//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/46px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="500" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/PEZY_Computing" class="mw-redirect" title="PEZY Computing">PEZY Computing</a>/<a href="/w/index.php?title=Exascaler_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Exascaler Inc. (page does not exist)">Exascaler Inc.</a></td>/n<td align="left">1</td>/n<td>0.2</td>/n<td>178,107</td>/n<td>395,264</td>/n<td>262,784</td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan"><img alt="Taiwan" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Acer_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Acer Group">Acer Group</a></td>/n<td align="left">1</td>/n<td>0.2</td>/n<td>177,100</td>/n<td>231,859</td>/n<td>26,244</td>/n</tr>/n</table>/n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Applications">Applications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Supercomputer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Applications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>/n<p>The stages of supercomputer application may be summarized in the following table:</p>/n<table class="wikitable">/n<tr>/n<th>Decade</th>/n<th>Uses and computer involved</th>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td>1970s</td>/n<td>Weather forecasting, aerodynamic research (<a href="/wiki/Cray-1" title="Cray-1">Cray-1</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td>1980s</td>/n<td>Probabilistic analysis,<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> radiation shielding modeling<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/CDC_Cyber" title="CDC Cyber">CDC Cyber</a>).</td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td>1990s</td>/n<td>Brute force code breaking (<a href="/wiki/EFF_DES_cracker" title="EFF DES cracker">EFF DES cracker</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td>2000s</td>/n<td>3D nuclear test simulations as a substitute for legal conduct <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_Non-Proliferation_Treaty" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear Non-Proliferation Treaty">Nuclear Non-Proliferation Treaty</a> (<a href="/wiki/ASCI_Q" class="mw-redirect" title="ASCI Q">ASCI Q</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td>2010s</td>/n<td>Molecular Dynamics Simulation (<a href="/wiki/Tianhe-1A" class="mw-redirect" title="Tianhe-1A">Tianhe-1A</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></td>/n</tr>/n</table>/n<p>The IBM <a href="/wiki/Blue_Gene" title="Blue Gene">Blue Gene</a>/P computer has been used to simulate a number of artificial neurons equivalent to approximately one percent of a human cerebral cortex, containing 1.6 billion neurons with approximately 9 trillion connections. The same research group also succeeded in using a supercomputer to simulate a number of artificial neurons equivalent to the entirety of a rat's brain.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>/n<p>Modern-day weather forecasting also relies on supercomputers. The <a href="/wiki/National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration">National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration</a> uses supercomputers to crunch hundreds of millions of observations to help make weather forecasts more accurate.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>/n<p>In 2011, the challenges and difficulties in pushing the envelope in supercomputing were underscored by <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>'s abandonment of the <a href="/wiki/Blue_Waters" title="Blue Waters">Blue Waters</a> petascale project.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>/n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Simulation_and_Computing_Program" title="Advanced Simulation and Computing Program">Advanced Simulation and Computing Program</a> currently uses supercomputers to maintain and simulate the United States nuclear stockpile.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>/n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_and_development_trends">Research and development trends</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Supercomputer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Research and development trends">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>/n<div class="thumb tright">/n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2x2x2torus.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/2x2x2torus.svg/220px-2x2x2torus.svg.png" width="220" height="191" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/2x2x2torus.svg/330px-2x2x2torus.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/2x2x2torus.svg/440px-2x2x2torus.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="485" data-file-height="420" /></a>/n<div class="thumbcaption">/n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2x2x2torus.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>/nDiagram of a three-dimensional <a href="/wiki/Torus_interconnect" title="Torus interconnect">torus interconnect</a> used by systems such as Blue Gene, Cray XT3, etc.</div>/n</div>/n</div>/n<p>Given the current speed of progress, industry experts estimate that supercomputers will reach 1&#160;<a href="/wiki/Exascale_computing" title="Exascale computing">EFLOPS</a> (10<sup>18</sup>, 1,000 PFLOPS or one quintillion FLOPS) by 2018. The Chinese government in particular is pushing to achieve this goal after they achieved the most powerful supercomputer in the world with <a href="/wiki/Tianhe-2" title="Tianhe-2">Tianhe-2</a> since 2013. Using the <a href="/wiki/Intel_MIC" class="mw-redirect" title="Intel MIC">Intel MIC</a> multi-core processor architecture, which is Intel's response to GPU systems, SGI also plans to achieve a 500-fold increase in performance by 2018 in order to achieve one EFLOPS. Samples of MIC chips with 32 cores, which combine vector processing units with standard CPU, have become available.<sup id="cite_ref-MIC2011_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MIC2011-103">[103]</a></sup> The Indian government has also stated ambitions for an EFLOPS-range supercomputer, which they hope to complete by 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-india-exa_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-india-exa-104">[104]</a></sup> In November 2014, it was reported that India is working on the fastest supercomputer ever, which is set to work at 132&#160;EFLOPS.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>/n<p>Erik P. DeBenedictis of <a href="/wiki/Sandia_National_Laboratories" title="Sandia National Laboratories">Sandia National Laboratories</a> theorizes that a zettaFLOPS (10<sup>21</sup>, one sextillion FLOPS) computer is required to accomplish full <a href="/wiki/Weather_forecasting" title="Weather forecasting">weather modeling</a>, which could cover a two-week time span accurately.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (January 2014)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup> Such systems might be built around 2030.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>/n<p>Many <a href="/wiki/Monte_Carlo_method" title="Monte Carlo method">Monte Carlo simulations</a> use the same algorithm to process a randomly generated data set; particularly, <a href="/wiki/Integro-differential_equation" title="Integro-differential equation">integro-differential equations</a> describing <a href="/wiki/Transport_phenomena" title="Transport phenomena">physical transport processes</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Random_walk" title="Random walk">random paths</a>, collisions, and energy and momentum depositions of neutrons, photons, ions, electrons, etc. <span id="dimension2016-01-29"></span>The next step for microprocessors may be into the <a href="/wiki/Three-dimensional_integrated_circuit" title="Three-dimensional integrated circuit">third dimension</a>; and specializing to Monte Carlo, the many layers could be identical, simplifying the design and manufacture process.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>/n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy_use">Energy use</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Supercomputer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Energy use">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>/n<p>High performance supercomputers usually require high energy, as well. However, Iceland may be a benchmark for the future with the world's first zero-emission supercomputer. Located at the Thor Data Center in <a href="/wiki/Reykjavik" class="mw-redirect" title="Reykjavik">Reykjavik</a>, Iceland, this supercomputer relies on completely renewable sources for its power rather than fossil fuels. The colder climate also reduces the need for active cooling, making it one of the greenest facilities in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>/n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_fiction">In fiction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Supercomputer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: In fiction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>/n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/AI_takeover" title="AI takeover">AI takeover</a></div>/n<p>Many <a href="/wiki/Science-fiction" class="mw-redirect" title="Science-fiction">science-fiction</a> writers have depicted supercomputers in their works, both before and after the historical construction of such computers. Much of such fiction deals with the relations of humans with the computers they build and with the possibility of conflict eventually developing between them. Some scenarios of this nature appear on the <a href="/wiki/AI_takeover" title="AI takeover">AI-takeover</a> page.</p>/n<p>Examples of supercomputers in fiction include <a href="/wiki/Multivac" title="Multivac">Multivac</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Machine_Stops" title="The Machine Stops">The Machine Stops</a>, <a href="/wiki/GLaDOS" title="GLaDOS">GLaDOS</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Evitable_Conflict" title="The Evitable Conflict">The Evitable Conflict</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vulcan%27s_Hammer" title="Vulcan's Hammer">Vulcan's Hammer</a>.</p>/n<h2><span
